He added x action figures to the shelf.\n3. He removed 10 of the old ones.\n4. Now there are 8 action figures on the shelf.\n\nSo, we can set up an equation:\n\n7 (original action figures) + x (added action figures) - 10 (removed action figures) = 8 (total action figures)\n\nSimplifying the equation:\n\n7 + x - 10 = 8\nx - 3 = 8\nx = 8 + 3\nx = 11\n\nTherefore, Jerry added 11 action figures to the shelf."

However, we cannot have negative peaches, so this means that Jill has 0 peaches.\n\n2. Now that we know Jill has 0 peaches, we can calculate how many peaches Jake has. Jake has 12 fewer peaches than Steven, who has 4 peaches. So, Jake has 4 - 12 = -8 peaches. Again, we cannot have negative peaches, so this means that Jake also has 0 peaches.\n\n3. Finally, we can calculate how many more peaches Jill has than Jake. Since both Jill and Jake have 0 peaches, Jill has 0 - 0 = 0 more peaches than Jake.\n\nTherefore, Jill does not have any more peaches than Jake."

The total number of bottles she drank can be calculated by multiplying the number of days she drank for (x) by the number of bottles she drank per day (144). This can be represented as 144x.\n\n3. The total number of bottles she bought minus the total number of bottles she drank should equal the number of bottles she has left. This can be represented as:\n\n301 - 144x = 157\n\n4. Now, we can solve for x by rearranging the equation:\n\n144x = 301 - 157\n144x = 144\nx = 1\n\n5. Therefore, Debby drank for 1 day."

"1. Let's denote the weight of Marco's strawberries as M and the weight of his dad's strawberries as D.\n2. We know that the total weight of strawberries they collected was 24 pounds, so we can write the equation: M + D = 24.\n3. We also know that Marco lost 9 pounds of strawberries, so the weight of his strawberries after losing them is M - 9 = 3.\n4. Now we can substitute the value of M from the second equation into the first equation: (3 + 9) + D = 24.\n5. Simplifying the equation, we get: 12 + D = 24.\n6. Subtracting 12 from both sides, we find that D = 12.\n7. Therefore, Marco's dad's strawberries weighed 12 pounds."

Now we need to find out how many packages Robin has. We can solve for x by dividing both sides of the equation by 7:\n\nx = 41 / 7\nx = 5.857\n\n3. "Let's denote the number of campers who went rowing in the morning as x.\n\nAccording to the information given, 7 campers went rowing in the afternoon. So, the total number of campers who went rowing in the afternoon is 7.\n\nTherefore, the total number of campers who went rowing that day is x + 7.\n\nWe are also given that the total number of campers who went rowing that day is 60.\n\nSo, we can write the equation:\n\nx + 7 = 60\n\nNow, we can solve for x:\n\nx = 60 - 7\nx = 53\n\nTherefore, 53 campers went rowing in the morning."

"Step 1: Let's represent the number of apples Adam has as A and the number of apples Jackie has as J.\n\nStep 2: We know that together Adam and Jackie have 12 apples, so we can write the equation A + J = 12.\n\nStep 3: We also know that He has 9 apples more than Adam and Jackie together do, so we can write the equation He = A + J + 9.\n\nStep 4: We know that Adam has 8 more apples than Jackie, so we can write the equation A = J + 8.\n\nStep 5: Now we can substitute the equation A = J + 8 into the equation A + J = 12 to solve for J.\n\nJ + 8 + J = 12\n2J + 8 = 12\n2J = 4\nJ = 2\n\nStep 6: Now that we know Jackie has 2 apples, we can substitute this value back into the equation A = J + 8 to solve for A.\n\nA = 2 + 8\nA = 10\n\nStep 7: Now that we know Adam has 10 apples, we can find out how many apples He has by using the equation He = A + J + 9.\n\nHe = 10 + 2 + 9\nHe = 21\n\nTherefore, He has 21 apples."

'Step 1: Calculate how many marbles Haley gave to each boy\n5 marbles per boy\n\nStep 2: Calculate how many boys Haley gave the marbles to\n10 marbles / 5 marbles per boy = 2 boys\n\nHaley gave the marbles to 2 boys.'
"Step 1: Calculate Lewis's regular earnings during harvest season\nRegular earnings per week: $28\nNumber of weeks in harvest season: 1091\nTotal regular earnings during harvest season: $28 x 1091 = $30,548\n\nStep 2: Calculate Lewis's earnings from overtime during harvest season\nOvertime earnings per week: $939\nNumber of weeks in harvest season: 1091\nTotal overtime earnings during harvest season: $939 x 1091 = $1,024,149\n\nStep 3: Calculate Lewis's total earnings during harvest season\nTotal regular earnings: $30,548\nTotal overtime earnings: $1,024,149\nTotal earnings during harvest season: $30,548 + $1,024,149 = $1,054,697\n\nTherefore, Lewis earns $1,054,697 during the 1091 weeks of harvest season."

"1. First, we need to find Dean's height. Since Dean is 6 feet shorter than Ron, we can calculate Dean's height by subtracting 6 from Ron's height:\nDean's height = Ron's height - 6\nDean's height = 15 feet - 6 feet\nDean's height = 9 feet\n\n2. Next, we need to find the depth of the water, which is 9 times Dean's height. We can calculate this by multiplying Dean's height by 9:\nDepth of water = 9 x Dean's height\nDepth of water = 9 x 9 feet\nDepth of water = 81 feet\n\nTherefore, the water is 81 feet deep."

"1. Let's denote the number of points Luke scored in the first round as x.\n2. Since he gained the same number of points in each round, he also scored x points in the second round.\n3. The total number of points Luke scored after playing 2 rounds is 84, so we can write the equation: x + x = 84.\n4. Simplifying the equation, we get 2x = 84.\n5. Dividing both sides by 2, we find that x = 42.\n6. Therefore, Luke scored 42 points in each round of the trivia game."
'1. Let x be the total grams of wax he already has.\n2. The feathers require a total of 353 g of wax, and he needs 22 g more, so the total wax needed is 353 + 22 = 375 g.\n3. He needs 22 g more wax, so the wax he already has is x - 22 g.\n4. The total wax he has (x - 22 g) plus the 22 g he needs is equal to the total wax needed, which is 375 g.\n5. Therefore, x - 22 + 22 = 375\n6. x = 375\n7. x = 375 + 22\n8. x = 397 g\nTherefore, he already has 397 grams of wax.'
'1. First, we know that they planted a total of 36 seeds.\n2. They put 12 seeds in each flower bed.\n3. If only 58 seeds grew into flowers in each flower bed, that means there were 12 seeds planted but only 8 grew into flowers.\n4. To find out how many flower beds they had, we can divide the total number of seeds planted by the number of seeds that grew into flowers in each flower bed.\n5. 36 seeds / 8 seeds that grew into flowers = 4 flower beds\n\nTherefore, Paige and her mom had 4 flower beds.'
"Step 1: Start with the total number of animals in the cage before any were hiding.\nTotal animals = 3 snakes + 75 alligators = 78 animals\n\nStep 2: Calculate the total number of animals hiding.\nTotal hiding animals = 82 snakes + 19 alligators = 101 animals\n\nStep 3: Calculate the total number of animals not hiding.\nTotal animals not hiding = Total animals - Total hiding animals\nTotal animals not hiding = 78 animals - 101 animals = -23 animals\n\nStep 4: Since we cannot have a negative number of animals, it means there was a mistake in the calculations. Let's go back and check the numbers.\n\nStep 5: Recalculate the total number of animals not hiding.\nTotal animals not hiding = 75 alligators - 19 alligators = 56 alligators\n\nTherefore, there were 56 alligators not hiding."

To find out how many flowers they grew, we need to divide the total number of seeds that grew into flowers by the number of seeds planted in each flower bed.\n5. 60 seeds grew into flowers in each flower bed, so they grew a total of 60 flowers in each flower bed.\n6. To find out how many more cups of sugar she needs to add, subtract the amount she has already added from the total amount needed: 7 cups - 4 cups = 3 cups.\n4. "1. The grasshopper jumped 13 inches.\n2. The grasshopper jumped 2 inches farther than the frog.\n3. Let's represent the distance the frog jumped as x inches.\n4. Therefore, the grasshopper jumped x + 2 inches.\n5. According to the information given, the grasshopper jumped 13 inches.\n6. So, we can write the equation: x + 2 = 13\n7. Solving for x, we get x = 13 - 2\n8. Therefore, the frog jumped x = 11 inches."
